<div id="review_1684561520" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1684561520" />
    <a title="Jan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57282794-jan"><img alt="Jan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505016022p2/57282794.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1684561520?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jan" href="/user/show/57282794-jan">Jan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57282794-jan?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1684561520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer653390291815403750">3.5 stars. I liked, but didn't *love* it. I had read and enjoyed this book a number of years ago and decided to give it another try. I recently read its sequel (for the first time!), <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/958521.The_Last_Hellion__Scoundrels___4_' title='The Last Hellion (Scoundrels, #4) by Loretta Chase' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Last Hellion</a>, and really liked it, so I went in feeling hopeful. And yes, I did enjoy Lord Of Scoundrels again this time. But for me it wasn't quite as good as The Last Hellion.<br/><br/>I know this is Ms Chase's most popular book, and many put it in their top ten of all HRs. And in many ways it is a rollicking, fun read </span>
  <span id="freeText653390291815403750" style="display:none">3.5 stars. I liked, but didn't *love* it. I had read and enjoyed this book a number of years ago and decided to give it another try. I recently read its sequel (for the first time!), <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/958521.The_Last_Hellion__Scoundrels___4_" title="The Last Hellion (Scoundrels, #4) by Loretta Chase" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Hellion</a>, and really liked it, so I went in feeling hopeful. And yes, I did enjoy Lord Of Scoundrels again this time. But for me it wasn't quite as good as The Last Hellion.<br /><br />I know this is Ms Chase's most popular book, and many put it in their top ten of all HRs. And in many ways it is a rollicking, fun read with two likeable MCs who go on a journey of love and self-discovery together. <br /><br />Sebastian, the lord of scoundrels himself, is the passionate, larger-than-life, half-Italian half-English Marquess of Dain. His father was a distant and bitter older man who had no idea how to love his son. His mother was a young, passionate Italian woman trapped in a loveless marriage. When she eventually runs off with someone else, little Sebastian is left lonely, bereft and confused. Then he is sent to school where he is bullied mercilessly. No wonder he grows up into a pleasure-seeking care-for-nobody.<br /><br />Until he meets Jessica. Clever, bold and sexy (but still an unmarried virgin) Jessica is more than a match for the passionate Marquess. <br /><br />The plot is interesting and moves along nicely. I particularly enjoyed the later section where <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Dain is reunited with his bastard son. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This was handled sensitively, and the conclusion of the book is quite satisfying.<br /><br />So, why didn't I like it as much as The Last Hellion? Why only 3.5 stars? Well, I think it was the overall tone of the book. EVERYTHING was larger-than-life and over-the-top. A bit too much melodrama for me. Yes, I liked both Jess and Dain, and their relationship worked. But it was all a bit too, too much, and their characters were actually a bit exhausting. For example, when Jess <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[shot Dain. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I mean, come on. That was pretty ridiculous. If things had been toned down just a little, then I think I would have felt a lot more involved in this book instead of feeling like a slightly bemused outsider watching these crazy antics. <br /><br />But, having said that, I understand that although I didn't like some aspects, that's not the case for everyone, as is obvious from the book's enduring popularity. So, if you haven't read it yet, why not try it for yourself and see? Ms Chase is a very capable writer, and I certainly intend to try more of her books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="653390291815403750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15438473303150040610" style="display:none"><b>Many literary awards and many glowing reviews for this historical romance.       <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Didi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Didi" href="/user/show/6082482-didi">Didi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=alpha-male">alpha-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer772338555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13064662235878259967">4 STARS<br/><br/>This book has been sitting on my trb shelf for a while now and I was only reminded of it by other GR friends reading it. Well, I'm glad I did! It was very well written and featured one of the most compelling Hero's I've ever read.<br/>Lord Dain, or Sebastian Ballister, is probably the most tortured, most interesting yet one of the most singularity attractive and sexy male leads around. Even if this is HR, his characterization is timeless. His upbringing was tragic, what, with a distant and rut</span>
  <span id="freeText13064662235878259967" style="display:none">4 STARS<br /><br />This book has been sitting on my trb shelf for a while now and I was only reminded of it by other GR friends reading it. Well, I'm glad I did! It was very well written and featured one of the most compelling Hero's I've ever read.<br />Lord Dain, or Sebastian Ballister, is probably the most tortured, most interesting yet one of the most singularity attractive and sexy male leads around. Even if this is HR, his characterization is timeless. His upbringing was tragic, what, with a distant and ruthless father who hated his sons very presence, to a young and tormented mother who felt the need to abandon her child to save her own sanity.<br /><br />Being made to feel different and odd, being made to feel unworthy for his mixed heritage was daunting at best. Never having someone to show him love and tell him it's okay to be different was unforgivable. Then to be shipped off to boarding school and be shunned by his father and bullied by his classmates...it's a miracle he didn't turn out worse than what he was. But Dain, as he was often called, had the backbone of stone, he didn't wither and perish, but grew stronger in the face of hate and carelessness. His heart was only buried beneath trauma, buried beneath a desire to protect oneself. Until the intelligent and beautiful Jessica came into his life.<br /><br />Jess was a fantastic heroine. She saw the beauty and strength of Dain right away. Beauty and the beast indeed! I loved how Dain was stunned to learn how she saw him: as a strong and virile, gorgeous male. That's fate right there. This was a very good HR, and despite Dain's despicable behaviour at times, I never hated him. I loved him through and through and felt he deserved his HEA more than the average guy. So glad he got it and to the most worthy of women! Everything really came full circle and I loved the ending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13064662235878259967" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38913081?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juliana Philippa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juliana Philippa" href="/user/show/1378820-juliana-philippa">Juliana Philippa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/9284218-lord-of-scoundrels">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=romance-historical">romance-historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=0-reviewed">0-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=2008-reads">2008-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=2008-jan-reads">2008-jan-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=0-to-reread">0-to-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=0-used-to-own">0-used-to-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=everyone-loved-it-am-odd-woman-out">everyone-loved-it-am-odd-woman-out</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38913081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2507738402636716298">I have to say that this was my first Loretta Chase romance, and though it didn't put me off the author completely, I definitely did not enjoy it as most everyone else seems to have. People seem to adore this book and I guess I just missed the boat on that one. <i>Lord of Scoundrels</i> was not at all horrible, though, which is why I plan to read more Loretta Chase before I make a definite decision on this author. As one other reviewer wrote, there was just something missing ... he was (mostly) great, s</span>
  <span id="freeText2507738402636716298" style="display:none">I have to say that this was my first Loretta Chase romance, and though it didn't put me off the author completely, I definitely did not enjoy it as most everyone else seems to have. People seem to adore this book and I guess I just missed the boat on that one. <i>Lord of Scoundrels</i> was not at all horrible, though, which is why I plan to read more Loretta Chase before I make a definite decision on this author. As one other reviewer wrote, there was just something missing ... he was (mostly) great, she was (mostly) great, but ... just little things here and there didn't quite fit right. It was like things almost hit the mark, but they never quite hit the center. For more details, see below. <br /><br /><i>SETTING: Paris, France and England (various locations), 1828</i><br /><br /><u>Summary (from the back cover)</u><br />"Tough-minded Jessica Trent's sole intention is to free her nitwit brother from the destructive influence of Sebastian Ballister, the notorious Marquess of Dain. She never expects to desire the arrogant, amoral cad. And when Dain's reciprocal passion places them in a scandalously compromising, and public, position, Jessica is left with no choice but to seek satisfaction ... <br /><br />Damn the minx for tempting him, kissing him ... and then forcing him to salvage her reputation! Lord Dain can't wait to put the infuriating bluestocking in her place - and in some amorous position. And if that means marriage, so be it! - though Sebastian is less than certain he can continue to remain aloof ... and steel his heart to the sensuous, headstrong lady's considerable charms."<br /><br /><u>Specifics</u> <br /><i>(* = kind of spoiler; ** = spoiler)</i><br />(1) I have read almost all the historical romances out there, and I know that you eventually see similar characters appearing here and there - it can't really be helped. I still don't like the cookie-cutter stereotyped characters, however, and Bertie Trent, Jessica's "nitwit" brother, is definitely one of those. Though somewhat humorous, the depiction of him as a thoughtless idiot passes into annoying exaggeration. He's an idiot - we get it - but such an idiot? Especially when Jessica and her grandmother seem to be such intelligent, engaging, sharp women? It was needed for the plot, I suppose, but grated on my nerves.<br /><br />(2) I found a problem of exaggeration with Dain's character also. Don't get me wrong, I love the whole "ridiculously horrible rake and scoundrel who is then reformed by love" as much as the next girl, but his was a little over the top. The near orgies and etc. - not needed. I liked the strength of his character, however, and disagree with one reviewer who thought him to be self-pitying; his childhood was extremely difficult and I thought it very believable that as an adult, his regular way to go about things in life is to shrug them off and laugh so that he is not hurt again. I'm a sucker for the tough-on-the-outside and vulnerable-underneath leading man, so I found that part of him appealing.<br /> <br />(3) I liked that Jessica was a strong woman who knew her own mind, but there was a certain something about her that got under my skin a little. It wasn't exactly snottiness or coldness or self-righteousness, but something close to these. <br /><br />(4) Kissing scene in the rain in Paris ... HOT!!! And then it was so cute after, when Sebastian watches Jessica leave a party and longs for her. ::sigh:: <br /><br />**(5) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Really didn't like Dain's attitude towards Dominick, his illegitimate son. He's wonderful at the end, but in the beginning, his attitude and actions really turned me off. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />*(6) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The parallel made between Dain's mother, who left him behind so he would be safe and provided for, and Charity Graves, who kept her son with her and look what happened ... I found it an unnecessary stretch. It is horrible that Sebastian's mother was married to a man old enough to be her father, but she didn't really seem like a very good mother to begin with, and the fact that she left him alone with his father, when she knew what a cold and horrible man her husband was, was not something that I view as easily forgivable, which is how Jessica tries to depict it. It's understandable, but that doesn't make it right, and I was kind of surprised that she's turned into this heroic figure, with her painting hung in the dining room and etc. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />**(7) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The subplot with Beaumont seemed completely forced, and I didn't really understand where the extreme animosity stemmed from. I know there was the incident where Dain caught him spying through a peephole when Dain was going to sleep with a prostitute in France, but even taking that into account, no interactions between Beaumont and Dain seemed like they were enough to create that type of hatred on the part of the former. The involvement of Vawtry and Charity and then the attempt to steal the icon - it was all unnecessary, in my opinion. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><u>Bottom Line</u><br />If you have an afternoon free and feel like reading a relatively enjoyable romance, then I suggest you borrow <i>Lord of Scoundrels</i> from a friend or get it from the library. Basically, if I had the chance again, I wouldn't buy it, as it won't be a re-read for me.<br /><br /><i>(Written January 8, 2008)</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2507738402636716298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780380776160" href="/book/show/3907970-lord-of-scoundrels">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45167578" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5940301975075409141">Having read this book praised all over the net, I confess I was a bit afraid of being disappointed. In the end, I WAS somewhat disappointed, because it didn´t wowed me as much as I expected. I really liked LOS, but it's not my #1 all-time favorite book.<br/><br/>What I loved:<br/><br/>1- The hero and the heroine, Jessica and Dain, were not like the standard characters so common in historical romances, that is, the gorgeous hero and the naive heroine. From the beginning, I was captivated by characters who "broke the</span>
  <span id="freeText5940301975075409141" style="display:none">Having read this book praised all over the net, I confess I was a bit afraid of being disappointed. In the end, I WAS somewhat disappointed, because it didn´t wowed me as much as I expected. I really liked LOS, but it's not my #1 all-time favorite book.<br /><br />What I loved:<br /><br />1- The hero and the heroine, Jessica and Dain, were not like the standard characters so common in historical romances, that is, the gorgeous hero and the naive heroine. From the beginning, I was captivated by characters who "broke the mold", so to speak. I particularly loved Jessica and her honest acceptance of her attraction to Dain.<br /><br />2- The dialogue was amazing. Jessica and Dain's interactions were very amusing and I found myself laughing several times.<br /><br />3- LC's writing style was paced with witty and funny remarks, that kept the story flowing seamlessly.<br /><br />What I didn't like (and prevented LOS from being a keeper):<br /><br />1- To put it simply, I had some problems with Dain's sometimes "childish" behavior towards Jessica (okay, it was funny at first, but enough is enough and it only made him look stupid in the end). His inital refusing to accept his bastard son wasn't something to be admired either.<br /><br />2- The secondary characters, especially that awful Beaumont and that silly Ainswood, were like "caricatures" and didn´t have much depth.<br /><br />All things considered, it was still a book worth reading and I had a pleasant time doing it. :)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5940301975075409141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_59266426" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/59266426" />
    <a title="Rane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1987431-rane"><img alt="Rane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419878997p2/1987431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">romance readers who love a great story!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=keeper">keeper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=historical">historical</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer59266426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15411286304051578575">When I picked up this book, I thought I would be in for a dark romance of two lonely people. What I got is two of the best characters in romance.<br/><br/> This book had me laughing at times that I would re-read the passage for another laugh. It had some of the best banter between two characters I’ve ever read and two complex yet simple leads you could understand on a very human level. <br/><br/> <br/>Beelzebub...er. I mean Dain came across as a selfish, hard nosed, vain, self-center man who could care and do less for a</span>
  <span id="freeText15411286304051578575" style="display:none">When I picked up this book, I thought I would be in for a dark romance of two lonely people. What I got is two of the best characters in romance.<br /><br /> This book had me laughing at times that I would re-read the passage for another laugh. It had some of the best banter between two characters I’ve ever read and two complex yet simple leads you could understand on a very human level. <br /><br /> <br />Beelzebub...er. I mean Dain came across as a selfish, hard nosed, vain, self-center man who could care and do less for anyone but himself. After his bleak childhood he went out to prove to everyone he truly was a demon then demon Beelzebub. Then the armor around him started to crack and slowly your show a man that sees himself not vain, but very self-conscious about himself, you don’t see a man who is selfish but unsure about his feelings and how to act toward those he cares about. For so many years he’s hid behind the mask of no caring that when he starts to live without the mask he does everything in his power to hide.<br /><br /> Jessica to coin a phase “big surprises come in small packages” she stood up to this giant of a man and laughed in his face, she didn’t go weeping into her room while he rode away, she stood her ground and told him like it is. She was blunt, honest and had a big heart. She understood Dain better then he understood himself, but not without a few bumps along the way for sure. <br /><br /> The banter between them was awesome, either one let up and always ending up surprising you and each other with their actions. (I did love Dain’s mental dictionary and his additions to it) Jess calmed Dain fears about him hurting her calling himself a ox of a man to his dainty wife. His dainty spitfire of a wife taught him a thing or two. Dain was so unsure about himself and the way he acted toward his child thinking he killed him by just picking him up roughly, Jess being small didn’t mean she didn’t pack a big punch.<br /><br /> You could understand and really relate to Dain and Jess both having to deal with the people around them, judging them and misunderstanding them. But through each other and their feelings they both discovery something in each other they were both missing. Love. Understanding, things many people take for granted and your shown through Dain how much that effects him and Jess having to show him it was okay to feel that way, but always there to give him that extra push. <br /><br /> Overall: an excellent romance about two very unlikely people finding the path to love through fears, a lot of humor and bumps in the road but finding their in the end!<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="15411286304051578575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_15023933" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15023933" />
    <a title="Julianna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/883725-julianna"><img alt="Julianna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442976820p2/883725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/15023933?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julianna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julianna" href="/user/show/883725-julianna">Julianna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Regency Romance Fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/883725-julianna?shelf=desert-island-keepers">desert-island-keepers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/883725-julianna?shelf=read-2007">read-2007</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/883725-julianna?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer15023933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15999090140766368024">Reviewed for <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.thcreviews.com'>www.thcreviews.com</a><br/><br/>I absolutely loved <i>Lord of Scoundrels</i>. This was my first reading of a Loretta Chase novel, and I will definitely be seeking out other books written by her in the future. Jessica was an extraordinary heroine who had a near perfection that one does not often find in a romance novel. Independent heroines can often become irritating to me, but Jessica was a thorough delight, a wonderful mix of charm, wit, strength, and heartfelt devotion. In spite of his utterly debauc</span>
  <span id="freeText15999090140766368024" style="display:none">Reviewed for <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.thcreviews.com">www.thcreviews.com</a><br /><br />I absolutely loved <i>Lord of Scoundrels</i>. This was my first reading of a Loretta Chase novel, and I will definitely be seeking out other books written by her in the future. Jessica was an extraordinary heroine who had a near perfection that one does not often find in a romance novel. Independent heroines can often become irritating to me, but Jessica was a thorough delight, a wonderful mix of charm, wit, strength, and heartfelt devotion. In spite of his utterly debauched nature early on, I still found Dain to be a completely sympathetic hero. I thought it was really sweet that Dain could be so worldly and yet so insecure as to be reluctant to bed his new bride. I also loved the vulnerability he showed when he really started opening up to Jess. Jessica's grandmother, Genevieve, was a delightful secondary character who was full of wit and charm herself. The settings and characterizations were very well drawn, and the pacing was wonderful. <i>Lord of Scoundrels</i> is the third book in the <i>Scoundrels</i> series, and introduces us to Vere Mallory, the Duke of Ainswood, who becomes the hero of book #4, <i>The Last Hellion</i>. Comte d’Esmond, who is the hero of book #2, <i>Captives of the Night</i> also plays a small secondary role. I believe that <i>Captives of the Night</i> and <i>Lord of Scoundrels</i> basically take place simultaneously, but <i>Captives of the Night</i> was written first. The first book of the series is <i>The Lion's Daughter</i>. I found <i>Lord of Scoundrels</i> to be a thoroughly enjoyable book, that has definitely earned a place on my keeper shelf.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15999090140766368024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_61695474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/61695474" />
    <a title="Summer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2274107-summer"><img alt="Summer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591129956p2/2274107.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/61695474?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Summer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Summer" href="/user/show/2274107-summer">Summer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780380776160" href="/book/show/3907970-lord-of-scoundrels">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2274107-summer?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2274107-summer?shelf=19th-century">19th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2274107-summer?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2274107-summer?shelf=france">france</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2274107-summer?shelf=hero-is-a-jerk">hero-is-a-jerk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2274107-summer?shelf=england">england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2274107-summer?shelf=victorian-period">victorian-period</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61695474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17773774785913031364">Once again I've read a book that I've forgotten I've already read. Thankfully I barely remember much from it so I didn't know what was going to happen for the most part. <br/><br/>Generally speaking the first 150 pages of this book was magic. The lady Jessica Trent comes from a noble, if eccentric, family. Her grandmother is a famous 'femme fatale' whom even now is still getting marriage offers. Jessica herself is not a young maiden but is constantly getting marriage offers due to her beauty and rich fami</span>
  <span id="freeText17773774785913031364" style="display:none">Once again I've read a book that I've forgotten I've already read. Thankfully I barely remember much from it so I didn't know what was going to happen for the most part. <br /><br />Generally speaking the first 150 pages of this book was magic. The lady Jessica Trent comes from a noble, if eccentric, family. Her grandmother is a famous 'femme fatale' whom even now is still getting marriage offers. Jessica herself is not a young maiden but is constantly getting marriage offers due to her beauty and rich family. She has a knack for picking out antiques or disregarded objects that are undervalued and selling them for a profit. Not something a normal lady of the time usually does. But it's her brother that's the real trouble. He doesn't have a sensible bone in his body. He drinks himself senseless and tends to gamble himself into quite a large amount of debt. Most of this debt is due to his idolization of Sebastian Ballister, the Marquess of Dain. Sebastian father also came from a long and proud family however his mother came from a noble family from Florentine, Italy. His mother was never accepted by his father and in turn his mother wasn't very motherly towards Sebastian. He's had a difficult childhood which has hardened him into a beast of a man. But once he meets Jessica that begins to change. Sebastian has vowed never to never let any woman get close to him but suddenly it's him who want's to be close. <br />The dialogue is witty and fun and the characters are interesting. I loved the scene with them in the rain especially. Sebastian has some of those romance 'misunderstandings' but otherwise those pages are great.<br /><br />As I said before, Sebastian has the typical romance 'misunderstandings' where he does unkind things toward the heroine because of his misguided assumptions. I assumed that that would end at a certain part of the book. However that assumption didn't hold true. Sebastian keeps acting like a brute towards Jessica. He gets himself into a brawl and drinks himself senseless on their wedding night, he decides he doesn't want to consummate the marriage all of a sudden due to some crazy fear he'll hurt her in the act, Jessica finally seduces him into taking her but afterward Sebastian deliberately acts callus towards her, only showing affection when making love. Then Jessica meets Sebastian's child out of wedlock. She doesn't hold it against Sebastian and wants them to keep the child since it looks like he isn't being cared for well. Not only does Sebastian disregard the child as some 'bastard son of a whore' he want's nothing to do with, he also disregards Jessica's feelings and continues to treat her terribly. It's Jessica who goes out and tries to contact the boy. It get's resolved by the end, and there are some really cute scenes with Sebastian and his boy but it's not until the very end of the book. Sebastian doesn't even admit to Jessica that he loves her until literally 3 pages before the end of the book. <br />It just really bothered me having a supposed 'hero' ignore his own son as call him trash, especially when his own childhood was traumatic and in many ways similar. <br />I know this is a very popular book, and I thought the first part of the book was really wonderful. I think I read a review on the 'Smart Bitches, Trashy Books' blog for 'Claiming the Courtesan' and the chief problem they had with the book was the lack of groveling. The hero does all these mean things to the heroine and all the hero says to apologize is a lame 'I'm sorry' and that's it. I think that's the same problem I had with this book too. I know in romance novels sometimes the hero doesn't always act so heroic. But the romance comes when he see's the error of his ways and begs for forgiveness. He becomes a changed man, so to speak. But in here he doesn't really change, he just says a lame 'I'm sorry' and not even until the last few pages of the book. <br /><br />I do want to try other books by this author since I hear such good things about her. I just wasn't as impressed by this book as I'd hoped. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17773774785913031364" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_786494125" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/786494125" />
    <a title="Katrina Passick Lumsden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden"><img alt="Katrina Passick Lumsden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416959676p2/1964146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/786494125?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katrina Passick Lumsden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katrina Passick Lumsden" href="/user/show/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden">Katrina Passick Lumsden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer786494125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13121050372691590753">Yowza. LOTS of angst in this here missive. Lots. So if you're not into angst, well... <br/><br/>I want to say I hated the hero. I want to. But I didn't hate him. Perhaps I SHOULD have, but I found myself instead curiously pondering the marked differences between cultures. Dain's mother was a spirited, passionate young Italian woman, and her temperament catastrophically clashed with that of her much older, stodgy English husband who assumed his firebrand of a wife was a bride of Satan. The result ended up </span>
  <span id="freeText13121050372691590753" style="display:none">Yowza. LOTS of angst in this here missive. Lots. So if you're not into angst, well... <br /><br />I want to say I hated the hero. I want to. But I didn't hate him. Perhaps I SHOULD have, but I found myself instead curiously pondering the marked differences between cultures. Dain's mother was a spirited, passionate young Italian woman, and her temperament catastrophically clashed with that of her much older, stodgy English husband who assumed his firebrand of a wife was a bride of Satan. The result ended up being a child no one apparently wanted, who was shunned, ignored, neglected, and outright emotionally abused by two completely selfish, emotionally unstable parents. He is then further subjected to scorn and ridicule by his peers at school. Is it any wonder, then, that Dain's emotional maturation ceased somewhere around pre-adolescence? Indeed, he's a 30-something with the emotional maturity of a 10 year old boy. And Loretta Chase wrote him masterfully. The reader gets to see every little confusing facet of his inner conflict. I loved it. <br /><br />Jessica Trent, conversely, is almost more mature than she should be. I loved her, as well. She has the sort of no-nonsense maternal air that Dain needs, and the two of them get caught up in their mutual attraction while neither has any idea what to do about it. There's a constant push and pull between the two that adds to the sexual tension, and their intelligent bantering is downright inspired. I liked that Jessica was willing to give Dain some latitude and understanding while not allowing him to walk all over her. Indeed, the more she figures him out, the more she's able to anticipate what he'll need, and when that happens, he begins to trust her, thus opening himself to further discovery. Watching their relationship develop was amazing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13121050372691590753" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1609041196" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1609041196" />
    <a title="Chitra *CJ*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46841583-chitra-cj"><img alt="Chitra *CJ*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479390580p2/46841583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1609041196?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chitra *CJ*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chitra *CJ*" href="/user/show/46841583-chitra-cj">Chitra *CJ*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46841583-chitra-cj?shelf=wicked-banter">wicked-banter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46841583-chitra-cj?shelf=v-card">v-card</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46841583-chitra-cj?shelf=smitten">smitten</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46841583-chitra-cj?shelf=tearjerker">tearjerker</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46841583-chitra-cj?shelf=scarred-disability">scarred-disability</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46841583-chitra-cj?shelf=im-the-lioness-hear-me-roar">im-the-lioness-hear-me-roar</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46841583-chitra-cj?shelf=shitz-and-giggles">shitz-and-giggles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46841583-chitra-cj?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46841583-chitra-cj?shelf=book-husbands">book-husbands</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46841583-chitra-cj?shelf=pure-insanity">pure-insanity</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1609041196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7534694694680384501"><i>
  <b>He went to work with speedy efficiency on the other glove. “I must be besotted,” he said evenly. “I have the imbecilic idea that you’re the prettiest girl I’ve ever seen. Except for your coiffure,” he added, with a disgusted glance at the coils and plumes and pearls. “That is ghastly.”<br/><br/>She scowled. “Your romantic effusions leave me breathless.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>"Lord of Scoundrels" is the story of Jessica and Dain.<br/><br/>I am so glad I've finally reached this milestone. This book had featured in over hundred listopia</span>
  <span id="freeText7534694694680384501" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>He went to work with speedy efficiency on the other glove. “I must be besotted,” he said evenly. “I have the imbecilic idea that you’re the prettiest girl I’ve ever seen. Except for your coiffure,” he added, with a disgusted glance at the coils and plumes and pearls. “That is ghastly.”<br /><br />She scowled. “Your romantic effusions leave me breathless.”</b>
</i><br /><br />"Lord of Scoundrels" is the story of Jessica and Dain.<br /><br />I am so glad I've finally reached this milestone. This book had featured in over hundred listopias and recommendations I had got since I started reading romance ages ago- now that I have read it- I am equally impressed.<br /><br />It begins with our charming and headstrong heroine, Jessica Trent trying to to free her nitwit brother Bertie from the destructive influence of Sebastian Ballister, the notorious Marquess of Dain. But it is easier said than done. Her brother idolizes the charming womanizer, until Jessica herself decides to take him on. Meeting him at an antiques and artistry shop, she shocks him by buying and obscene watch, and soon bidding on an ugly but rare painting. <br />Soon they engage in a battle of wills, which begins with words but soon turns into much more. The chemistry is instant, and both appear to be struck by mutual lust. The heroine challenges the hero and his ego, somehow picking at his hidden wounds, and he devises retribution by carefully planning a seduction and public humiliation. However, the retaliation comes when our heroine, a skilled markswoman shoots the hero in a public gaming house, and leaves him febrile and suffering. A lawyer is involved, a marriage proposition is made and accepted, a duel is fought, debauching ensues and the second half of the book deals with their life after the wedding.<br />We then move on to the heroine trying to pry open the hero's closed off heart with her giant cupid arrow. Be it slowly making his hurt inner child emerge, uninhibitedly seducing him, fighting for her marital rights, confessing her love without conditions or punishing him with silence, she is the perfect antidote for his very poisoned soul.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>She shook her head. “No, and if’s not because I’m addled upstairs, either. You are not to think I’m mad, Dain, because I’m not. I know it looks that way, but there’s a perfectly reasonable explanation. The intellect, as you of all men ought to know, is no match for the intensity of the animal drive. I’ve been in lust with you from the moment I met you.”<br /><br />His knees grew wobbly. He crouched down in front of her and took a firm grip of the edge of the mattress. He cleared his throat. “Lust.” He managed to keep the one syllable low and steady. He decided not to try any more syllables of anything.</b>
</i><br /><br />I think this was one of my favorite scenes in the book- the heroine confessing her lust for the hero from the moment she met him, hence showing him she was truly his soulmate- as the feeling had been reciprocated. Their lovemaking scenes were insanely sexy and well written, be it first seduction, the wild sex behind the rhododendrons or the intimate bedtime confessions.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>He looked down into her smiling countenance. “Interesting, indeed. The Bane and Blight of the Ballisters, Lord of Scoundrels himself. The greatest whoremonger in Christendom. A cocksure, clod-pated ingrate.”<br /><br />“The wickedest man who ever lived.”<br /><br />“A great gawk of a lummox. A spoiled, selfish, spiteful brute.”<br /><br />She nodded. “Don’t leave out ‘conceited clod-pole.’”</b>
</i><br /><br />He referred to her as "Nitwit, Sapskull, Termagant, Ruthless, Vicious, Fiendish" etc, while she called him "Beelzebub, blockhead, clodpole" etc. They challenged each other's wits at every turn, and their passionate banters were oh so much fun to read.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>And in Lord Beelzebub’s dark, harsh Dartmoor of a heart, the sweet rain fell and a seedling of love sprouted in the once barren soil.</b>
</i><br /><br />The book is also moderately good on angst, with the introduction of Dominick in the last few chapters, and how the hero deals with his present, his past and unresolved feelings. I think his scenes with him could be have been more detailed, but I found them equally heartbreaking and cute.<br /><br />I found this very special as it is set in Devon, Exeter and prominently features Dartmoor and Haytor rocks- coincidentally where I reside! If it wasn't for the CoVid 19, and my profession, I would totally have taken the bus to Dartmoor and reread this sweet book.<br /><br /><i>
  <b> “I love you, Sebastian Leslie Guy de Ath Ballister. I love you, Lord Dain and Beelzebub, Lord Blackmoor, Lord Launcells, Lord Ballister—”<br /><br />“That’s too many names,” he said. “We’ve been wed more than a month. Since it appears that you mean to stay, I might as well give you leave to call me by my Christian name. It is preferable, at any rate, to ‘clodpole ”<br /><br />“I love you, Sebastian,” she said.<br /><br />“I’m rather fond of you, too,” he said.<br /><br />“Immensely fond,” she corrected.</b>
</i><br /><br />I'd give this gem a definite five star. A kickass heroine who fought at every turn, stood toe to toe with our hero, was proud of her love and sexuality, fought for her rights, was selflessly devoted and a charming hellcat. A scarred, confident, ex-tomcatty hero who has a tragic past, is so determined to win but does not mind losing. A wonderfully passionate love story. A great ending.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“It is easy enough to calculate. One fertile marchioness plus one virile marquess equals a brat, sometime between Candlemas and Lady Day.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Safe<br />5/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="7534694694680384501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_537109369" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/537109369" />
    <a title="Varian Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5961603-varian-rose"><img alt="Varian Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357480487p2/5961603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/537109369?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Varian Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Varian Rose" href="/user/show/5961603-varian-rose">Varian Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780061753817" href="/book/show/10178512-lord-of-scoundrels">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5961603-varian-rose?shelf=hero-is-a-jerk">hero-is-a-jerk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5961603-varian-rose?shelf=one-star">one-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5961603-varian-rose?shelf=everyone-loves-it-but-me">everyone-loves-it-but-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5961603-varian-rose?shelf=potato-rage">potato-rage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5961603-varian-rose?shelf=rage-inducing">rage-inducing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5961603-varian-rose?shelf=ugh-that-was-awful">ugh-that-was-awful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5961603-varian-rose?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5961603-varian-rose?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5961603-varian-rose?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5961603-varian-rose?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer537109369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14122496773881556271">This...I wanted to love it. I was told over and over again how awesome it was. Like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/360259.Flowers_from_the_Storm' title='Flowers from the Storm by Laura Kinsale' rel='nofollow noopener'>Flowers from the Storm</a>, they said...they lied. This was nothing like Flowers.<br/><br/>Reading this book was like listenng to bad black metal. It was like expecing the majesty, atmospehere and emotion of Limbonic Art's <i>Moon In The Scorpio</i>, only to get a bad Cradle of Filth ripoff instead.<br/><br/>I was told that this was the book to give non-romance readers who were curious about the genre. No. This book reads like a parody of the </span>
  <span id="freeText14122496773881556271" style="display:none">This...I wanted to love it. I was told over and over again how awesome it was. Like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/360259.Flowers_from_the_Storm" title="Flowers from the Storm by Laura Kinsale" rel="nofollow noopener">Flowers from the Storm</a>, they said...they lied. This was nothing like Flowers.<br /><br />Reading this book was like listenng to bad black metal. It was like expecing the majesty, atmospehere and emotion of Limbonic Art's <i>Moon In The Scorpio</i>, only to get a bad Cradle of Filth ripoff instead.<br /><br />I was told that this was the book to give non-romance readers who were curious about the genre. No. This book reads like a parody of the romance genre. It has every chiche I can think of in romance and flat characters as well. <br />--A heroine who's smart, beautiful, witty and has many many marriage proposals--but won't marry for some reason that doesn't fit the era the book takes place in, and readers do not understand.<br />--A hero who's "tortured" by things that happened many years ago and can only be changed by the power of lurrrrve.<br />--The constant bickering between hero/heroine that eventually leads to love because all those arguments hid what they were really feeling!<br /><br />This was awful. I gave it 98 pages and gave up when Jessica shot Dain. She shot him. With a postol. Pistols from that time period were well known for misfiring (so he's very lucky to be hit in the arm) and he was certin to have an infection. And this is treated as funny and empowering to women?!? I...just can't...<br /><br />Then there was the language anachronisms. I counted at leas 14 obvious ones in the pages I read. <br /><br />Jess didn't fit the time frame at all. I know the reader was supposed to admire her, but I didn't. She struck me as a selfish judgmental twat who didn't give a damn what others thought of her.<br /><br />The hero, Dain, was a childish brat who knew he was acting like a child but would't change his ways. I dod not feel sorry for him in the least.<br /><br />They deserve each other.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14122496773881556271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_78086372" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78086372" />
    <a title="FlibBityFLooB" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2505272-flibbityfloob"><img alt="FlibBityFLooB" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262459297p2/2505272.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78086372?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="FlibBityFLooB" class="user" itemprop="url" name="FlibBityFLooB" href="/user/show/2505272-flibbityfloob">FlibBityFLooB</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2505272-flibbityfloob?shelf=witty-i-am-not">witty-i-am-not</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2505272-flibbityfloob?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2505272-flibbityfloob?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2505272-flibbityfloob?shelf=era-regency-pre-victorian">era-regency-pre-victorian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78086372" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7062450343959678043">The first half of this book was a lot of fun to read, right up until the point where the heroine pulled a gun on the hero. From that point, I began to question my sanity in reading the book, as well as my own comprehension of the English language.<br/><br/>What, you ask, would cause me to wonder if I understood English? Well, you're reading this, so I will share a few choice sentences from the book:<br/><br/><i>
  <b>"What the Bane and Blight of the Ballisters was, at the moment, was terrified."</b>
</i> (pg 173 in my copy). Umm</span>
  <span id="freeText7062450343959678043" style="display:none">The first half of this book was a lot of fun to read, right up until the point where the heroine pulled a gun on the hero. From that point, I began to question my sanity in reading the book, as well as my own comprehension of the English language.<br /><br />What, you ask, would cause me to wonder if I understood English? Well, you're reading this, so I will share a few choice sentences from the book:<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"What the Bane and Blight of the Ballisters was, at the moment, was terrified."</b>
</i> (pg 173 in my copy). Ummmm... Huh? That sentence made me feel drunk and I had to re-read it several times. Yes, I finally understood the sentence, but I think it would have made more sense if she had simply said something like: At the moment, the Bane and Blight of the Ballisters family was terrified. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>"Nuss give it to you when your ma run off, 'n you was sick some'at fierce from it"</b>
</i> (pg 315 in my copy). Again... what? I don't get it.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"'N I was to tell Her Ladyship that she done what Her Ladyship said - tole the boy some'at or other like Her Ladyship asked her to."</b>
</i> (pg 333 in my copy) Okay, that was just a weird sentence. hmmm...<br /><br />In addition, I wasn't crazy about some of the so-called romantic scenes in this book... Take for instance:<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"He trailed his tongue over one sleek eyebrow"</b>
</i> (pg 247 in my copy). What!?!?!? Is the hero a cat? Is he going to have hairballs later? I would be mighty weirded out if my husband started licking my eyebrows. hehehehhehe<br /><br />And, from a scene in the heat of passion, we are treated to the following dialogue: <i>
  <b>"Yes, Kill me, Jess. Do it again."</b>
</i> (pg 345 in my book) Very odd thing to say when involved in relations with your spouse. <br /><br />Apparently, lots of people really liked this book. Maybe I really am insane. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7062450343959678043" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1673788209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15742448035714537445">This is still my favorite historical romance after so many years. The rereading can still make me laugh so hard throughout the book. I'm in love with both the characters. The hero and heroine are such a unique and refreshing characters to all the other stereotypical reform rake and blushing virgin. I just can't get enough of Dain and Jessica!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

		<td>
		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('u51no8Pj5BaSsKy3XFzngKresGLxaGy1KxEsmJMZyhB5hp37I/l9LiVk3icVcQknDQvUhT+UY1KWWrfpE44aeA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5peGXZBR5BG9iFqm2ShIfxebVhgH1SeYNBysIFdU6q8kjHwFcEt9KQpcKDaQBabYsE4y/8kpKH+JVzdR18M6xw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10959713863828423089">Loretta Lynda Chekani was born in 1949, of Albanian ancestry. For her, the trouble started when she learned to write in first grade. Before then, she had been making up her own stories but now she knew how to write them down to share. In her teenage years, she continue to write letters, keep a journal, write poetry and even attempt the Great American Novel (still unfinished). She attended New Engl</span>
  <span id="freeText10959713863828423089" style="display:none">Loretta Lynda Chekani was born in 1949, of Albanian ancestry. For her, the trouble started when she learned to write in first grade. Before then, she had been making up her own stories but now she knew how to write them down to share. In her teenage years, she continue to write letters, keep a journal, write poetry and even attempt the Great American Novel (still unfinished). She attended New England public schools, before she went off to college and earned an English degree from Clark University.<br /><br />After graduation, she worked a variety of jobs at Clark including a part-time teaching post. She was also moonlighting as a video scriptwriter. It was there that she met a video producer who inspired her to write novels and marry him. Under her married name, Loretta Chase, has been publishing historical romance novels since 1987. Her books have won many awards, including the Romance Writers of America RITA.</span>
